     <p>In the last six years, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.provost.harvard.edu/institutional_research/Provost_-_Harvard_Fact_Book_2009-10_FINAL_new.pdf">Harvard's student population</a> ranged between 19,000 and 21,000, across all programs. Harvard enrolled 6,655 students in undergraduate programs, 3,738 students in graduate programs, and 10,722 students in professional programs.<sup id="cite_ref-Head_count_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Head_count-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> The undergraduate population is 51% female, the graduate population is 48% female, and the professional population is 49% female.<sup id="cite_ref-Head_count_122-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Head_count-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Undergraduate admission to Harvard is characterized by the Carnegie Foundation as &quot;more selective, lower transfer-in&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_59-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> Harvard College received 27,462 applications for admission to the Class of 2013, 2,175 were admitted (7.9%), and 1,658 enrolled (76.2%).<sup id="cite_ref-CDS_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> 95% of first year students graduated in the top tenth of their high school class.<sup id="cite_ref-CDS_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> Harvard also enrolled 266 <a href="/wiki/National_Merit_Scholar" title="National Merit Scholar" class="mw-redirect">National Merit Scholars</a>, the most in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> 88% of students graduate within 4 years and 98% graduate within 6 years.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Harvard College accepted 5.8% of applicants for the class of 2017, a record low for the school's entire history.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> The number of acceptances has gone down since the university announced a large increase in financial aid in 2008.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Harvard College ended its early admissions program in 2007 as the program was believed to disadvantage low-income and under-represented minority applicants applying to selective universities.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> For the Class of 2016 an Early Action program was reintroduced. The undergraduate admissions office's <a href="/wiki/Legacy_preferences" title="Legacy preferences">preference for children of alumni</a> policies have been the subject of scrutiny and debate as it primarily aids whites and the wealthy and seems to conflict with the concept of meritocratic admissions.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty_and_staff">Faculty and staff</span></h3> 
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" style=""> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" /></a></td> 
        <td class="mbox-text" style=""><span class="mbox-text-span">This section requires <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Harvard_University&amp;action=edit">expansion</a>. <small><i>(August 2010)</i></small></span></td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>Harvard's faculty includes scholars such as biologist <a href="/wiki/E._O._Wilson" title="E. O. Wilson">E. O. Wilson</a>, cognitive scientist <a href="/wiki/Steven_Pinker" title="Steven Pinker">Steven Pinker</a>, physicists <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Randall" title="Lisa Randall">Lisa Randall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roy_Glauber" title="Roy Glauber" class="mw-redirect">Roy Glauber</a>, chemists <a href="/wiki/Elias_Corey" title="Elias Corey" class="mw-redirect">Elias Corey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dudley_R._Herschbach" title="Dudley R. Herschbach">Dudley R. Herschbach</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_M._Whitesides" title="George M. Whitesides">George M. Whitesides</a>, computer scientists <a href="/wiki/Michael_O._Rabin" title="Michael O. Rabin">Michael O. Rabin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Valiant" title="Leslie Valiant">Leslie Valiant</a>, Shakespeare scholar <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Greenblatt" title="Stephen Greenblatt">Stephen Greenblatt</a>, writer <a href="/wiki/Louis_Menand" title="Louis Menand">Louis Menand</a>, critic <a href="/wiki/Helen_Vendler" title="Helen Vendler">Helen Vendler</a>, historians <a href="/wiki/Henry_Louis_Gates,_Jr." title="Henry Louis Gates, Jr." class="mw-redirect">Henry Louis Gates, Jr.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Niall_Ferguson" title="Niall Ferguson">Niall Ferguson</a>, economists <a href="/wiki/Amartya_Sen" title="Amartya Sen">Amartya Sen</a>, <a href="/wiki/N._Gregory_Mankiw" title="N. Gregory Mankiw" class="mw-redirect">N. Gregory Mankiw</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Barro" title="Robert Barro">Robert Barro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_A._Marglin" title="Stephen A. Marglin" class="mw-redirect">Stephen A. Marglin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Don_M._Wilson_III" title="Don M. Wilson III">Don M. Wilson III</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martin_Feldstein" title="Martin Feldstein">Martin Feldstein</a>, political philosophers <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Mansfield" title="Harvey Mansfield">Harvey Mansfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shirley_Williams" title="Shirley Williams">Baroness Shirley Williams</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Sandel" title="Michael Sandel">Michael Sandel</a>, political scientists <a href="/wiki/Robert_Putnam" title="Robert Putnam" class="mw-redirect">Robert Putnam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Nye" title="Joseph Nye">Joseph Nye</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Hoffmann" title="Stanley Hoffmann">Stanley Hoffmann</a>, scholar/composers <a href="/wiki/Robert_D._Levin" title="Robert D. Levin">Robert Levin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Rands" title="Bernard Rands">Bernard Rands</a>, astrophysicist <a href="/wiki/Alyssa_A._Goodman" title="Alyssa A. Goodman">Alyssa A. Goodman</a>, and legal scholar <a href="/wiki/Alan_Dershowitz" title="Alan Dershowitz">Alan Dershowitz</a>.</p> 
     <p>Past faculty members include <a href="/wiki/Michael_Walzer" title="Michael Walzer">Michael Walzer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephan_Thernstrom" title="Stephan Thernstrom">Stephan Thernstrom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Nozick" title="Robert Nozick">Robert Nozick</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni">Notable alumni</span></h3> 
     <p>Politics: U.N. Secretary General <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a>; American political leaders <a href="/wiki/John_Hancock" title="John Hancock">John Hancock</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Adams" title="John Adams">John Adams</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Quincy_Adams" title="John Quincy Adams">John Quincy Adams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rutherford_B._Hayes" title="Rutherford B. Hayes">Rutherford B. Hayes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>; Chilean President <a href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A1n_Pi%C3%B1era" title="Sebasti&aacute;n Pi&ntilde;era">Sebasti&aacute;n Pi&ntilde;era</a>; Colombian President <a href="/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Santos" title="Juan Manuel Santos">Juan Manuel Santos</a>; Costa Rican President <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Figueres" title="Jos&eacute; Mar&iacute;a Figueres">Jos&eacute; Mar&iacute;a Figueres</a>; Mexican Presidents <a href="/wiki/Felipe_Calder%C3%B3n" title="Felipe Calder&oacute;n">Felipe Calder&oacute;n</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Harvard_Alum_apparent_new_president_of_Mexico_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harvard_Alum_apparent_new_president_of_Mexico-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Salinas_de_Gortari" title="Carlos Salinas de Gortari">Carlos Salinas de Gortari</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_la_Madrid" title="Miguel de la Madrid">Miguel de la Madrid</a>; Mongolian President <a href="/wiki/Tsakhiagiin_Elbegdorj" title="Tsakhiagiin Elbegdorj">Tsakhiagiin Elbegdorj</a>; Peruvian President <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Toledo" title="Alejandro Toledo">Alejandro Toledo</a>; Taiwanese President <a href="/wiki/Ma_Ying-jeou" title="Ma Ying-jeou">Ma Ying-jeou</a>; Canadian Governor General <a href="/wiki/David_Lloyd_Johnston" title="David Lloyd Johnston" class="mw-redirect">David Lloyd Johnston</a>; Albanian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Fan_S._Noli" title="Fan S. Noli">Fan S. Noli</a>; Canadian Prime Ministers <a href="/wiki/Mackenzie_King" title="Mackenzie King" class="mw-redirect">Mackenzie King</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Trudeau" title="Pierre Trudeau">Pierre Trudeau</a>; Greek Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Antonis_Samaras" title="Antonis Samaras">Antonis Samaras</a>; Israeli Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu" title="Benjamin Netanyahu">Benjamin Netanyahu</a>; former Pakistani Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Benazir_Bhutto" title="Benazir Bhutto">Benazir Bhutto</a>; U. S. Secretary of Housing and Urban Development <a href="/wiki/Shaun_Donovan" title="Shaun Donovan">Shaun Donovan</a>; Canadian political leader <a href="/wiki/Michael_Ignatieff" title="Michael Ignatieff">Michael Ignatieff</a>; Pakistani Members of Provincial Assembly <a href="/wiki/Murtaza_Bhutto" title="Murtaza Bhutto">Murtaza Bhutto</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sanam_Bhutto" title="Sanam Bhutto">Sanam Bhutto</a>.</p> 
     <p>Royals: <a href="/wiki/Frederik,_Crown_Prince_of_Denmark" title="Frederik, Crown Prince of Denmark">Frederik, Crown Prince of Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crown_Princess_Masako" title="Crown Princess Masako">Crown Princess Masako</a> of <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sheikh" title="Sheikh">Sheikh</a> Dr. <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Sabah_Al-Salem_Al-Sabah" title="Muhammad Sabah Al-Salem Al-Sabah">Muhammad Sabah Al-Salem Al-Sabah</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>.</p> 
     <p>Court: Israeli Supreme Court President <a href="/wiki/Aharon_Barak" title="Aharon Barak">Aharon Barak</a>.</p> 
     <p>Business: Religious leader, businessman &amp; philanthropist <a href="/wiki/Aga_Khan_IV" title="Aga Khan IV">Aga Khan IV</a>, businessman &amp; philanthropist <a href="/wiki/Bill_Gates" title="Bill Gates">Bill Gates</a>, philanthropist <a href="/wiki/Huntington_Hartford" title="Huntington Hartford">Huntington Hartford</a>, Facebook creator <a href="/wiki/Mark_Zuckerberg" title="Mark Zuckerberg">Mark Zuckerberg</a>, businessman&amp;financier <a href="/wiki/Scott_Mead" title="Scott Mead">Scott Mead</a>, and businessman <a href="/wiki/Gabe_Newell" title="Gabe Newell">Gabe Newell</a>.</p> 
     <p>Other fields: Civil rights leader <a href="/wiki/W._E._B._Du_Bois" title="W. E. B. Du Bois">W. E. B. Du Bois</a>; philosopher <a href="/wiki/Henry_David_Thoreau" title="Henry David Thoreau">Henry David Thoreau</a>; authors <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Waldo_Emerson" title="Ralph Waldo Emerson">Ralph Waldo Emerson</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_S._Burroughs" title="William S. Burroughs">William S. Burroughs</a>; educator <a href="/wiki/Harlan_Hanson" title="Harlan Hanson">Harlan Hanson</a>; poets <a href="/wiki/Wallace_Stevens" title="Wallace Stevens">Wallace Stevens</a>, <a href="/wiki/T._S._Eliot" title="T. S. Eliot">T. S. Eliot</a> and <a href="/wiki/E._E._Cummings" title="E. E. Cummings">E. E. Cummings</a>; conductor <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Bernstein" title="Leonard Bernstein">Leonard Bernstein</a>; cellist <a href="/wiki/Yo_Yo_Ma" title="Yo Yo Ma" class="mw-redirect">Yo Yo Ma</a>; comedian, television show host and writer <a href="/wiki/Conan_O%27Brien" title="Conan O'Brien">Conan O'Brien</a>; actors <a href="/wiki/Tatyana_Ali" title="Tatyana Ali">Tatyana Ali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matt_Damon" title="Matt Damon">Matt Damon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fred_Gwynne" title="Fred Gwynne">Fred Gwynne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hill_Harper" title="Hill Harper">Hill Harper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rashida_Jones" title="Rashida Jones">Rashida Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Lee_Jones" title="Tommy Lee Jones">Tommy Lee Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Judd" title="Ashley Judd">Ashley Judd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Lemmon" title="Jack Lemmon">Jack Lemmon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natalie_Portman" title="Natalie Portman">Natalie Portman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mira_Sorvino" title="Mira Sorvino">Mira Sorvino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elisabeth_Shue" title="Elisabeth Shue">Elisabeth Shue</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Scottie_Thompson" title="Scottie Thompson">Scottie Thompson</a>; film directors <a href="/wiki/Darren_Aronofsky" title="Darren Aronofsky">Darren Aronofsky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Terrence_Malick" title="Terrence Malick">Terrence Malick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mira_Nair" title="Mira Nair">Mira Nair</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Whit_Stillman" title="Whit Stillman">Whit Stillman</a>; television executive <a href="/wiki/Brian_Graden" title="Brian Graden">Brian Graden</a>; architect <a href="/wiki/Philip_Johnson" title="Philip Johnson">Philip Johnson</a>; musicians <a href="/wiki/Rivers_Cuomo" title="Rivers Cuomo">Rivers Cuomo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Morello" title="Tom Morello">Tom Morello</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gram_Parsons" title="Gram Parsons">Gram Parsons</a>; musician, producer and composer <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Leslie" title="Ryan Leslie">Ryan Leslie</a>; unabomber <a href="/wiki/Ted_Kaczynski" title="Ted Kaczynski">Ted Kaczynski</a>; programmer and activist <a href="/wiki/Richard_Stallman" title="Richard Stallman">Richard Stallman</a>; NFL quarterback <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Fitzpatrick" title="Ryan Fitzpatrick">Ryan Fitzpatrick</a>; NFL center <a href="/wiki/Matt_Birk" title="Matt Birk">Matt Birk</a>; NBA player <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Lin" title="Jeremy Lin">Jeremy Lin</a>; physician <a href="/wiki/Sachin_H._Jain" title="Sachin H. Jain">Sachin H. Jain</a>; physicist <a href="/wiki/J._Robert_Oppenheimer" title="J. Robert Oppenheimer">J. Robert Oppenheimer</a>; writer <a href="/w/index.php?title=Victor_W._Hwang&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Victor W. Hwang (page does not exist)">Victor W. Hwang</a>; and Tibetologist <a href="/wiki/George_de_Roerich" title="George de Roerich">George de Roerich</a>.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature_and_popular_culture">Literature and popular culture</span></h2> 
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-style" style=""> 
      <tbody>
       <tr>

         <div style="width: 52px;">

     </table> 
     <p>The perception of Harvard as a center of either elite achievement, or elitist privilege, has made it a frequent literary backdrop.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_literature">In literature</span></h3> 
     <ul> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Accidental_Billionaires" title="The Accidental Billionaires">The Accidental Billionaires</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Ben_Mezrich" title="Ben Mezrich">Ben Mezrich</a> is a narrative account of Facebook's founding set partially at Harvard</li> 
      <li><i>Hacking Harvard</i> is novel by <a href="/wiki/Robin_Wasserman" title="Robin Wasserman">Robin Wasserman</a>, a Harvard University alumna.</li> 
      <li>In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Handmaid%27s_Tale" title="The Handmaid's Tale">The Handmaid's Tale</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Atwood" title="Margaret Atwood">Margaret Atwood</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Post-apocalyptic" title="Post-apocalyptic" class="mw-redirect">post-apocalyptic</a> novel, much of the action takes place in Cambridge, with vaguely recognizable Harvard landmarks occasionally making their way into the narrator's place descriptions.</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Erich_Segal" title="Erich Segal">Erich Segal</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Love_Story_(1970_film)" title="Love Story (1970 film)">Love Story</a></i> (1970), which concerns a romance between a wealthy hockey player (<a href="/wiki/Ryan_O%27Neal" title="Ryan O'Neal">Ryan O'Neal</a>) and a brilliant Radcliffe student of modest means (<a href="/wiki/Ali_MacGraw" title="Ali MacGraw">Ali MacGraw</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> is screened annually for incoming freshmen.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Segal's <i><a href="/wiki/The_Class_(Erich_Segal_novel)" title="The Class (Erich Segal novel)">The Class</a></i> (1985) and <i><a href="/wiki/Doctors_(novel)" title="Doctors (novel)">Doctors</a></i> (1988) are also set at Harvard.</li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Paper_Chase_(novel)" title="The Paper Chase (novel)">The Paper Chase</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/John_Jay_Osborn,_Jr." title="John Jay Osborn, Jr.">John Jay Osborn, Jr.</a>, a 1970 novel adapted for a film and a television series based at Harvard Law School.</li> 
      <li><i>The Second Happiest Day</i> (1953) by &quot;John Phillips&quot; (John P. Marquand, Jr.) depicts the Harvard of the World War II generation.</li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Sound_and_the_Fury" title="The Sound and the Fury">The Sound and the Fury</a></i>, by <a href="/wiki/William_Faulkner" title="William Faulkner">William Faulkner</a>, features Quentin Compson's experiences at Harvard.</li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Women%27s_Room" title="The Women's Room">The Women's Room</a></i>, by <a href="/wiki/Marilyn_French" title="Marilyn French">Marilyn French</a>, largely features protagonist Mira's experiences at Harvard</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Pamela_Thomas-Graham" title="Pamela Thomas-Graham">Pamela Thomas-Graham</a>'s series of mystery novels (<i>Blue Blood</i>, <i>Orange Crushed</i>, and <i>A Darker Shade Of Crimson</i>), protagonist Nikki Chase is an African-American Harvard economics professor.</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Cecilia_Tan" title="Cecilia Tan">Cecilia Tan</a>'s romance novel series, commonly known as the &quot;Magic University series&quot; and including the books <i>The Siren and the Sword</i> and <i>The Tower and the Tears</i>, is set at the magical university hidden inside Harvard known as &quot;Veritas&quot;.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Onscreen">Onscreen</span></h3> 
     <p>Because Harvard generally forbids filming on its property, most scenes set at Harvard (especially indoor shots, but excepting aerial footage and shots of public areas such as Harvard Square) are in fact shot elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Paper_Chase_(film)" title="The Paper Chase (film)">The Paper Chase</a></i> (1973 film) and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Paper_Chase_(TV_series)" title="The Paper Chase (TV series)">The Paper Chase</a></i> (1978?79, 1983?86 TV series)</li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/Soul_Man_(film)" title="Soul Man (film)">Soul Man</a></i> (1986)</li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/With_Honors_(film)" title="With Honors (film)">With Honors</a></i> (1994)</li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/Good_Will_Hunting" title="Good Will Hunting">Good Will Hunting</a></i> (1997)</li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/Harvard_Man" title="Harvard Man">Harvard Man</a></i> (2001)</li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/How_High" title="How High">How High</a></i> (2001)</li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/Legally_Blonde" title="Legally Blonde">Legally Blonde</a></i> (2001)</li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/Stealing_Harvard" title="Stealing Harvard">Stealing Harvard</a></i> (2002)</li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Great_Debaters" title="The Great Debaters">The Great Debaters</a></i> (2007)</li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Social_Network" title="The Social Network">The Social Network</a></i> (2010)</li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/Suits_(TV_Series)" title="Suits (TV Series)" class="mw-redirect">Suits (TV Series)</a></i></li> 
     </ul>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span></h2> 
     <div class="reflist references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;"> 
      <ol class="references"> 
       <li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Harvard's <i>Veritas</i> appears on the university's arms; <a href="/wiki/Heraldry" title="Heraldry">heraldically</a> speaking, however, a 'motto' is a word or phrase displayed on a scroll in conjunction with a shield of arms. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=zkQWZaZqZfUC&amp;pg=PA330&amp;lpg=PA330#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=false">Since 1692</a> University <a href="/wiki/Seal_(device)" title="Seal (device)" class="mw-redirect">seals</a> have borne <i>Christo et Ecclesiae</i> (for Christ and the Church) in this manner, arguably making that phrase the university's motto in a heraldic sense. This legend is otherwise not in general use today.</span></li> 
       <li id="cite_note-founding-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-founding_2-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">An appropriation of &pound;400 toward a &quot;school or college&quot; was voted on October 28, 1636 (OS), at a meeting which convened on September 8 and was adjourned to October 28. Some sources consider October 28, 1636 (OS) (November 7, 1636 NS) to be the date of founding. Harvard's 1936 tercentenary celebration treated September 18 as the founding date, though 1836 bicentennial was celebrated on September 8, 1836. Sources: meeting dates, <span class="citation book">Quincy, Josiah (1860). <i>History of Harvard University</i>. 117 Washington Street, Boston: Crosby, Nichols, Lee and Co.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHarvard+University&amp;rft.aufirst=Josiah&amp;rft.aulast=Quincy&amp;rft.au=Quincy%2C+Josiah&amp;rft.btitle=History+of+Harvard+University&amp;rft.date=1860&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.place=117+Washington+Street%2C+Boston&amp;rft.pub=Crosby%2C+Nichols%2C+Lee+and+Co.&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?vid=OCLC11636583&amp;id=KynqxH_4lGUC&amp;pg=RA1-PA586&amp;lpg=RA1-PA586">p. 586</a>, &quot;At a Court holden September 8th, 1636 and continued by adjournment to the 28th of the 8th month (October, 1636)... the Court agreed to give &pound;400 towards a School or College, whereof &pound;200 to be paid next year....&quot; Tercentenary dates: <span class="citation news"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.time.com/time/magazine/printout/0,8816,756722,00.html">&quot;Cambridge Birthday&quot;</a>. <i>Time</i>. 1936-09-28<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved 2006-09-08</span>.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHarvard+University&amp;rft.atitle=Cambridge+Birthday&amp;rft.date=1936-09-28&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.time.com%2Ftime%2Fmagazine%2Fprintout%2F0%2C8816%2C756722%2C00.html&amp;rft.jtitle=Time&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span>: &quot;Harvard claims birth on the day the Massachusetts Great and General Court convened to authorize its founding. This was Sept. 8, 1637 under the Julian calendar. Allowing for the ten-day advance of the Gregorian calendar, Tercentenary officials arrived at Sept. 18 as the date for the third and last big Day of the celebration;&quot; &quot;on Oct. 28, 1636 ... &pound;400 for that 'school or college' [was voted by] the Great and General Court of the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Bay_Colony" title="Massachusetts Bay Colony">Massachusetts Bay Colony</a>.&quot; Bicentennial date: <span class="citation web">Marvin Hightower (2003-09-02). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.news.harvard.edu/gazette/2003/10.02/02-history.html">&quot;Harvard Gazette: This Month in Harvard History&quot;</a>. Harvard University<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved 2006-09-15</span>.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHarvard+University&amp;rft.aulast=Marvin+Hightower&amp;rft.au=Marvin+Hightower&amp;rft.btitle=Harvard+Gazette%3A+This+Month+in+Harvard+History&amp;rft.date=2003-09-02&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.news.harvard.edu%2Fgazette%2F2003%2F10.02%2F02-history.html&amp;rft.pub=Harvard+University&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span>, &quot;Sept. 8, 1836 - Some 1,100 to 1,300 alumni flock to Harvard's Bicentennial, at which a professional choir premieres &quot;Fair Harvard.&quot; ... guest speaker Josiah Quincy Jr., Class of 1821, makes a motion, unanimously adopted, 'that this assembly of the Alumni be adjourned to meet at this place on the 8th of September, 1936.'&quot; Tercentary opening of Quincy's sealed package: <i>The New York Times,</i> September 9, 1936, p. 24, &quot;Package Sealed in 1836 Opened at Harvard. It Held Letters Written at Bicentenary&quot;: &quot;September 8th, 1936: As the first formal function in the celebration of Harvard's tercentenary, the Harvard Alumni Association witnessed the opening by President Conant of the 'mysterious' package sealed by President Josiah Quincy at the Harvard bicentennial in 1836.&quot;</span></li>
